Finally, the examination of the availability of teaching-leaming materials and school environment shows
that the availability of more than 4 teaching-learning materials have a positive effect on the result of
Primary Education Certificate exam. However, it is important to mention that due to extreme shortages,
textbooks were not part of the package of teaching and learning material that was considered. The school
database contains information only on the existence of small school materials (such as rulers and boxes of
small weights), as well as the existence of facilities such as latrines, canteens and playgrounds. With
regard to the availability of small pedagogic materials, only the best endowed schools have significantly
better results. These schools represent 14% of the sample, while 60% of school in the sample have no
pedagogic materials at all. Similarly, the results are positively correlated with the condition of the school
building, the existence of a canteen and the existence of other facilities. The consideration of all the above
elements simultaneously (model not shown) confirms all the above findings, except the positive influence of
the partially qualified teacher. The positive influence of the French-speaking teachers is confirmed.
Despite the data limitations and methodological imperfections (particularly the fact that there was no
control of the students' socio-economic background), this analysis draws attention to a few interesting facts.
First, many of the findings are coherent with usual research findings. Second, they tend to support the
strategies and policies on which the ESDP was based, particularly the emphasis on teacher in-service
training to enhance their French language capability, the provision of pedagogic materials, the retrofitting
of schools with latrines and water, the planned slight decrease of average class size and teacher /per student
ratios, the use of multigrade classes, the limited recourse to double shifting and the emphasis on school
maintenance.

Annex 6: Procurement and Disbursement Arrangements
MAURITANIA: Education Sector Development Program
Procurement
General
1.    The Mauritanian procurement Code was prepared in 1993 and will be revised on the basis of the
recommendations of the CPAR, which was carried out in February 1999. In the event that national
procurement laws and procedures conflict with the IDA Guidelines for procurement, the Mauritanian
procurement code permits IDA procedures to take precedence over any contrary provisions in national law
and regulations.
2.    The 1999 CPAR includes recommendations to: (i) clarify the role of the Ministry in charge of
Public Works as regards its role of Maitre d 'Ouvrage for large works and Maitre d'Oeuvre for small
works, (ii) review the mandates of the Central Tender Board (CTB) and the Departmental Tender Board
(DTB) to allow the CTB to monitor DTB's performances; (iii) open publicly and simultaneously technical
and financial offers for works and goods; (iv) disclose the evaluation criteria in the bid documents, (v)
include the obligation of interets moratoires in the Code, and (vi) state that all imports under public
contracts will be subject to pre-boarding inspection.
3.    An IDF Grant was provided in 1998 to support modernization of the public procurement system
and to help the public procurement reform. This grant, managed by the MAED, aims at: (i) reinforcing
MAED's institutional capacity to support executing agencies in preparing and updating their procurement
plans and to monitor their implementation; (ii) reinforcing the CTB capacity to play its new role and to
develop its monitoring services; (iii) supporting the modemization of the public procurement law and
related by-laws; and (iv) helping the Government develop and implement a training program for
procurement staff.
Guidelines
4.    Procurement of goods and works financed by IDA will be carried out in accordance with the
Guidelines for procurement under IBRD loans and IDA credits published in 1995 and updated in
January and August 1996 and in September 1997 and January 1999. The Bank's standard bidding
documents for goods and civil works and the Standard Bid Evaluation Forms will be used. National
Competitive Bidding (NCB) advertised locally will be carried out in accordance with Mauritania's
procurement laws and regulation, acceptable to IDA, provided that: (i) bids are advertised in national
newspapers with a wide circulation; (ii) the bid document clearly explains the bid evaluation, award criteria
and bidder qualification; (iii) bidders are given adequate response time to prepare and submit bids
(minimum four weeks); (iv) technical and financial bids are publicly and simultaneously opened; (v) bids
are awarded to the lowest evaluated bidder; (vi) no eligible bidder is precluded from participation,
regardless of nationality; (vii) no domestic preference margins are applicable to domestic manufacturers or
suppliers; (viii) prior to issuing the first call for bids, a draft standard bidding document will be submitted
to and found acceptable by IDA. NCB managed by AMEXTIPE will be based on the Agency's standard
bidding documents for goods and civil works, recently approved by IDA (February 2001).
5.    The aggregate values for NCB and other non-ICB procurement methods for goods and works are
limitative and cannot be exceeded without the prior no-objection of the Bank. The DPEF will monitor such
- 79 -



procurement in order to alert the Bank in a timely manner when this may occur.
6.    Consultant services contracts financed by IDA will be procured in accordance with the Guidelines
for the Selection of Consultants by World Bank Borrowers published in January 1997 and updated in
September 1997 and January 1999. The Bank's Standard Request for Proposals: Selection of
Consultants, dated July 1997 and revised April 1998 and July 1999 and forms of contracts (lump-sum,
time based, and/or simplified contracts for short-term assignments and individual consultants) as well as
the Sample Form of Evaluation Report for Selection of Consultants will be used. Simplified contracts will
be used for short-term assignments, not exceeding six months, carried out by firms or individual
consultants.
Advertising
7.    A General Procurement Notice (GPN) will be prepared and published, following Board approval,
in the United Nations Development Business, listing all works contracts above US$250,000 equivalent,
goods contracts above US$100,000 equivalent, and large contracts for consultant services (above
US$100,000 equivalent), to obtain expressions of interest and to draw up a roster of reliable firms that will
make up the shortlists.
8.    The related bidding documents will not be released and neither will the shortlist of consultants be
prepared until eight weeks after the GPN has been published. The GPN will be updated annually for those
contracts still outstanding. A GPN will also be published in the national press for contracts to be awarded
under NCB. Specific Procurement Notices (SPNs) for goods and works will be advertised locally, and for
large contracts (ICB), intemationally. Sufficient time will be allowed to obtain the bid documents.
Procurement Implementation Arrangements
9.    Procurement activities for the first phase of the ESDP will be carried out by the Government for
the procurement financed by AfDB, IDA, IDB, and the 'Government budget, while bilateral donors, such as
FAC, intematiotial organizations, such as UNICEF, and NGOs, will maintain responsibility for
procurement of the contracts they finance.
10.   Procurement carried out by the Government will be handled by the following procurement
implementing agencies: (i) the existing DPEF, for the procurement of contracts of goods and services
financed by IDA, AfDB and IDB credits, and by the Government's counterparts to these credits and the
investment budget of the MEN; (ii) the DAFM, for all procurement financed under operating costs of the
MEN (except salaries); (iii) AMEXTIPE, by delegation from the MEN, for the procurement of works, with
the exception of primary classrooms and water supply facilities; and (iv) Communities for the procurement
of works and related furniture for primary schools financed by IDA and AfDB.
11.  The DPEF and DAFM work through the National Tender Board - Commission Centrale des
Marches (CCM), which is responsible for the procurement process for contracts exceeding 10 million UM
(US$40,000 equivalent); and through the Departmental Tender Board - Commission Departementale des
Marches (CDM) of their respective ministries for the procurement of contracts under this threshold but
exceeding I million UM (US$4,000 equivalent). The DPEF and DAFM prepare bidding documents but do
not award contracts. Awards are the responsibility of the CCM and the respective CDM. Contracts
exceeding 50 million UM (US$200,000 equivalent) must be approved by the Prime Minister in accordance
with national procurement procedures. These thresholds will be raised in the forthcoming revised code and
the maximum time allowed for clearances will be reduced. AMEXTIPE has its own procurement
- 80 -



commission. For IDA-financed contracts managed by AMEXTIPE and DPEF, the procurement process
(preparation of bidding documents, bid evaluation and award, contract management) will be carried out by
the agency itself and the relevant procurement commission, but liaison with IDA will be carried out through
the DPEF which will have the responsibility to monitor the whole procurement program.
Procurement Capacity Assessment, action plan, risk rating and thresholds
12.   A participatory procurement capacity assessment of the existing implementing agencies (DPEF,
DAFM, AMEXTIPE and Communities) was conducted during program preparation, with representatives
from the CTB-CCM, DPEF, DAFM and AMEXTIPE. The following four points emerged from this
assessment:
(a)    Strength and weaknesses of the four procurement agencies (DPEF, DAFM, AMEXTIPE and
communities) are as follows:
i. The DPEF has gained extensive experience in IDA and AfDB procurement procedures through
previous projects. It handled satisfactorily and simultaneously the IDA-supported General Education
Project (Cr. 2706-MAU) and Vocational Training Project (Cr. 2521-MAU). The unit is well
organized and has clearly defined procurement responsibilities and skilled staff. It has the capacity to
manage the Procurement Cycle well and has a very good record keeping system. However, DPEF
staffing is not sufficient to cope with: (i) the volume of contracts of the first phase of the ESDP which
is much larger than previous projects, as a consequence of the sector approach involving new
components such as higher education, school health, adult literacy and ECD; and (ii) the mandate to
assist in building the procurement capacity of the DAFM.
ii. The DAFM has a weak procurement capacity at present since recurrent budgets (aside from
personnel salaries) were very limited in the past, and procurement practices hardly ever involved open
competition. To cope with the significant increase in non-salary recurrent resources made available to
the MEN under ESDP for the purchase of educational goods related to the quality education objectives
(from 2,539 UM million in 1998 to 4,518 UM million in 2005); a strong DAFM's procurement
capacity needs to be built, almost from scratch. This capacity building is one of the key objectives of
the first phase of the ESDP supported by IDA's APL. Transfer to the MEN's DAFM of the
procurement activities presently handled by the MAED's DPEF is expected to take place during the
second phase of the ESDP, subject to a positive assessment of the capacity built in the DAFM during
the first phase.
iii. AMEXTIPE has good experience in IDA procurement procedures and adequate staffing to
manage contracts for the small works in Nouakchott and other cities. AMEXTIPE will be contracted
for the management of works in regional and provincial capitals. However the Agency is still weak
because of the large number of new staff who need to become procurement proficient. This weakness is
to be addressed through the parallel Urban Development Program (UDP) under preparation, which
includes an action plan for procurement training ofAMEXTIPE's staff before UDP credit
effectiveness, scheduled before the end of 2001.
iv. Communities will be handling procurement of goods and works under the school construction
program financed by IDA and AfDB. Communities developed the capacity to carry out this type of
procurement during the implementation of the Education III and V projects (financed by IDA and
l'Agence Franqaise de Developpement) when they built more than 2,500 classrooms with technical
assistance provided by three engineers and their assistants under contracts with the DPEF. A technical
- 81 -



evaluation of the current program shows that the quality of work was acceptable while the costs were
lower than comparable construction managed by other agencies in the country and even in other West
African countries. The operation manual for this component was revised during the program
preparation to include specific community-based procurement procedures, acceptable to IDA. Specific
assistance will continue to be provided to communities by the pool of engineers and assistants under the
previous contractual arrangements with the DPEF. This assistance will include information and
training of communities on community-based procurement.
(b)    Action plan to build procurement capacity. On the basis of the procurement capacity assessment,
an action plan has been incorporated into the program to build the long-term capacity of the MEN to
administer procurement. The objective is to bring the DAFM to full capacity during the first phase of the
ESDP while donor-financed procurement will be handled by the DPEF. During the second phase, all
procurement activities will be carried out by the DAFM. With respect to DAFM, the actions cover:
organization, staffing, training, equipment, and record keeping. These activities are detailed in a specific
module (GS2) of the PIP. With respect to DPEF, the actions cover: (i) recruitment and training of two
additional procurement specialists, and (ii) support to the above-mentioned capacity building of the DAFM.
The action plan for DPEF, which is essential for program implementation and should be in place before
procurement starts, is detailed in a specific action plan at the end of the procurement section of this annex.
Measures to strengthen the capacity of AMEXTIPE is incorporated in parallel Bank support (UDP).
(c)    Risk rating. During the first phase of ESDP, the bulk of the donor-financed procurement (about
80%) will be handled by the DPEF, which has a fair record in handling past donor-financed procurement.
Considering the immediate action plan to upgrade its capacity to the level required by ESDP, the DPEF
falls in the average-risk zone. AMEXTIPE, which will manage the civil works contracts with the
exception of wells and primary classrooms (representing 50% of the donor-financed construction in the first
phase), also have a fair past record and assessment rating. Given the parallel strengthening measures, the
Agency also falls into the average risk zone. According to its participatory assessment, the DAFM falls
into the high-risk zone, but a sub-component of the ESDP management component is specifically
addressing this issue. Given the communities' ten years' experience in community-based procurement
arrangements for primary classroom construction, they fall into low-risk zone. Based on the above, the
overall assessment of risk is average.
(d)    Threshold for prior reviews. Based on the above-mentioned risk rating and the past experience with
education projects in other countries, the thresholds for prior review will be set up, for the first phase of the
ESDP, as shown in Table B. The long-term objective of the ESDP is to strengthen the capacity of all
agencies and to move them gradually to the low-risk category. The second phase of the program may
consider raising these thresholds if the agencies meet specific performance indicators stated in the
Implementation Manual. The post-review will be applied to at least one in ten contracts not subject to prior
review.
Program Procurement Plan (PPP)
13.   The Borrower has prepared a draft detailed procurement plan for the first four-year phase of the
program, showing the step-by-step procedures for procurement, contract packages for goods, works and
consultant services, and the estimated costs for each package, procurement/selection method, and the
activities which follow procurement until completion. The PPP will cover Govemment-managed
procurement regardless of the origin of funds (IDA, AfDB, BCI, and recurrent budget). The procurement
plan, acceptable by the Bank, was submitted at negotiations. By November of each year, the DPEF will
submit to IDA for its non-objection, an updated version of the PPP with the actual procurement activities
- 82 -



for the past year and revisions of the plan for the following years.

14.   A draft Project Implementation Plan (PIP) -- Manuel d 'Execution - was developed during project
preparation on the basis of the draft Project Implementation Plan Guidelines issued in 1999 by the Project
Management Thematic Group of the Bank. The PIP is organized in 19 modules corresponding to
sub-components, plus specific Manuals of Procedures governing each grant mechanism (below referred in
para 28) including the community-based primary construction program. Each PIP module includes the
specific procurement section for the module, specific responsibilities for commitment and implementation,
and identifies the risks that need to be minimized. The Manual of Procedures for the community-based
primary construction program was deemed satisfactory to the Bank at project appraisal subject to minor
improvements which were done before negotiations. The 19 modules of the PIP were reviewed at
negotiations and Bank's comments provided to the borrower. Submission of the final version of the PIP is
a condition of effectiveness. Submission of the Manuals of Procedures satisfactory to the Bank, for all
grants mechanism, with the exception of the Manual goveming the community-based construction program,
is a condition of disbursement for these grants.
15.   Manuel des Procedures Administratives, Financieres et Comptables. The borrower has recruited
a consultant to prepare this Manual. Offers will be opened on august 2001 and the consultant work will
start in September 2001. This Manual will reiterate the procurement arrangements described in this Annex.
Submission of the Manual of Administrative, Financial and Accounting Procedures, acceptable to IDA is a
condition of effectiveness.
Works
16.    ESDP program. During the first phase of the ESDP (2001-2005), the construction program
totaling US$67.67 million equivalent (all sources of funds included) encompasses: (a) ECD: construction of
a central ECD training center and construction/rehabilitation of 13 regional training centers, (b) primary
education: (i) the primary school building program detailed in para. 17 below, and (ii) expansion of the ENI
in Nouakchott; (c) lower secondary education: construction of 36 new small-scale colleges mainly in
villages, and of 250 classrooms, 28 administrative blocs, 135 computer rooms, about 60 libraries and
laboratories, and 80 sanitation blocs in existing schools; rehabilitation of 260 classrooms and about 350
sanitation blocs; (d) upper secondary: construction of 50 laboratories, 15 libraries and 70 computer rooms
and as many sanitation blocs; rehabilitation of 100 classrooms and 35 sanitation blocs; (e) vocational
training: rehabilitation and expansion of existing training centers; construction of the office-building of the
new INP-FTP; (f) higher education: rehabilitation/expansion of the CUR in Rosso; (g) management:
construction of 29 IDENs and 2 DRENs and expansion of 8 DREFs, construction of an administrative
building for Examination Offices; and rehabilitation of the MEN central offices. The ESDP construction
program will be supported by IDA, among other donors.
17.    The primary school building program of the ESDP totalling US$19.81 million equivalent includes
(all sources of funds): (i) construction of about 2,730 classrooms as follows: 1,800 small schools
- 83 -



comprising up to 3 classrooms will be built as a matter of priority in order to deliver 6 grades of education
through multigrade teaching; and 930 dilapidated sub-standard classrooms, built with non-permanent
materials, will be reconstructed; (ii) rehabilitation of 460 classrooms; (iii) completion of all new
3-classroom schools and retrofitting of existing ones with latrines (about 1,340), office-storage blocs
(about 1,100), fencing (about 800), and water supply facilities (about 1,000). With the exception of the
provision of water to schools, which will be executed by the Direction de l'Hydraulique (US$1.07 million
equivalent), the implementation of the school-building program will be delegated to communities through
the community-based construction program detailed in para 26(a) below (for a total of US$17.74 million
equivalent).
Contracts for Works supported by IDA (total contracts equivalent to US$11.85 million)
18.    Scope. Works financed under the proposed IDA credit will comprise: (a) ECD: central and
regional training centers, (b) primarv education: water supply to 500 schools; (c) lower secondary
education: construction of 16 new small colleges, 87 classrooms and computer rooms, 28 administrative
blocs, and rehabilitation of 128 existing classrooms and 355 existing sanitation blocs; (d) upper secondary:
rehabilitation of 100 classrooms and 35 sanitation blocs; (e) vocational training: rehabilitation of 16
existing vocational training centers and construction of the office-building for the new INP-FTP; (f)
management: construction of 17 IDENs and 2 DRENs and expansion of 8 DREFs to accommodate
DRENs, construction of an Examination Office, and rehabilitation of the MEN central office building. The
remainder of the construction program is expected to be financed by the Govermment, mainly from the
additional resources provided by the HIPC initiative, and by other donors, mainly AfDB and IDB.
19.    Procurement Methods. Civil works contracts exceeding US$250,000 equivalent will be procured
through International Competitive Bidding (ICB). Contracts below this threshold will be procured under
National Competitive Bidding (NCB) up to an aggregate amnount of US$ 10.20 million equivalent.
Contracts for school construction/rehabilitation of secondary schools, training centers, and administrative
offices scattered throughout the country, will be procured by a Contract Management Agency (CMA), the
AMEXTIPE. The CMA will apply provisions of schedule 3 of the Development Credit Agreement (DCA)
for procurement procedures. Standard Bidding Documents for NCB set up in the most recent AMEXTIPE
Procedures Manual (dated June 2000), which have been found acceptable to IDA will be used for the
delegated sub-program. Any changes and revisions in the Procedures Manual will be subject to IDA prior
review. Works for water supply to rural schools will be executed by the Direction de l'Hydraulique
through force account for a maximum total amount of US$1.07 million equivalent under an Agreement
with the DPEF. Contracts for small works estimated to cost less than US$30,000 equivalent per contract,
up to an aggregate amount of US$0.57 million equivalent, may be procured under lump-sum fixed-priced
contracts awarded on the basis of written quotations from three reputable small local contractors. The
invitation shall include a detailed description of the works, basic specifications, the required completion
period, a basic form of agreement acceptable to IDA, and relevant drawings when applicable. The award
will be made to the contractor whose submission is substantially acceptable, who offers the lowest price
quotation for the required work, and has the experience and resources to complete the contract successfully.
The contracts will mostly be for works related to small construction and rehabilitation, such as ECD
centers and rehabilitation of existing facilities in remote areas. The above-mentioned aggregate value limits
for NCB and small works cannot be exceeded without prior IDA non-objection. The DPEF will maintain a
monitoring system, including contracts managed by AMEXTIPE to alert the Bank when these limits may
be exceeded and will ask the Bank for advice beforehand.
- 84 -



Goods
20.   During the first phase of the ESDP (2001-2005), goods to be procured for the program (all sources
of funds) total US$51.66 million equivalent.
Contracts for goods supported by IDA (total contracts equivalent to US$14.22 million)
21.   Scope. Goods to be financed under the IDA credit will include: (i) furniture for new and
rehabilitated facilities; (ii) office equipment: computers, photocopiers, and other equipment for the existing
and new offices; (iii) textbooks, instructional materials and library books for primary and secondary
schools, University and teacher training institutes, including transportation services for the goods; (iv)
pedagogic materials for ECD; (v) computers for secondary schools; (vi) equipment for laboratories and
science teaching in secondary and higher education; (vii) retrofitting the secondary schools with adequate
furniture; (viii) technical equipment for renovated vocational training centers; (ix) drugs and supplementary
nutrients; (x) information systems (including MIS and GIS software and hardware) for the entire education
sector; and (xi) equipment for monitoring and supervision: vehicles and spare parts for the management
units at the central and decentralized levels of the MEN and for the new INP-FTP.
22.   Procurement methods. Goods to be financed under the IDA credit will be grouped into packages of
at least US$100,000 equivalent to be procured through International Competitive Bidding in accordance
with the World Bank's Guidelines. Information Systems will be procured through ICB on the basis of the
Bank's Standard Bidding Document entitled: Supply and Installation of Information Systems published in
February 1999. Contracts for goods that have to be purchased on an annual basis, and for other goods and
equipment, available on the local market at a competitive price, with a unit value exceeding US$30,000
equivalent and which cannot be grouped together into packages exceeding US$100,000 equivalent and
which are unlikely to be of interest to foreign suppliers because of their small size and the geographical
dispersion of the delivery points, will be awarded on the basis of National Competitive Bidding in
accordance with procedures acceptable to IDA, up to an aggregate amount of US$1.39 million equivalent.
Small quantities of drugs and micronutrients estimated to cost less than US$100,000 equivalent per
contract, will be procured from United Nation Agencies (WHO or UNICEF) up to an aggregate amount of
US$0.37 million equivalent. International Shopping will be used for off-the-shelf goods that cannot be
grouped into lots of US$100,000 equivalent, and are not available on the local market, such as books and
instructional materials, up to an aggregate amount of US$0.74 million equivalent. Small quantities of
off-the-shelf goods such as office supplies, consumable materials and spare parts considered to be standard
items locally available, and which cannot be grouped together into packages of at least US$30,000
equivalent, will be purchased through National Shopping provided that the aggregate amount of such
contracts does not exceed US$0.31  million equivalent. National and International Shopping solicitations
will: (a) be issued in writing to at least three reputable suppliers; (b) include specifications and, if goods are
not immediately available, the delivery time; (c) give the estimated cost, including cost of inland
transportation and insurance; (d) be opened at the same time for evaluation; and (e) in the case of
International Shopping, be solicited from at least three suppliers in two different countries. The
above-mentioned aggregate value limits for NCB, International and National Shopping are limitative and
cannot be exceeded without prior IDA non-objection. The DPEF will maintain a tracking system to alert
the Bank when these limits may be exceeded and will ask the Bank for advice beforehand.
Consultant services (US$ 21.22 million equivalent)
23.   Consulting services for the PNDSE will be mainly financed by: (i) the French Cooperation which
- 85 -



has a large network of technical assistance across MEN's subsectors; (ii) AfDB and IDB for services
related to the investment program they support; (iii) UNICEF for the literacy and Mahadras component;
and (iii) IDA for consulting services necessaxy to implement successfully the ESDP and that are not
provided by other partners.
Contracts for consultant services supported by IDA (total contracts US$7.91 million equivalent)
24.    Scope. IDA-financed consultant services will be for: (a) preparation of engineering designs for
works, bid documents and works supervision; (b) studies for: (i) textbook editing policy; (ii) student flow
regulation in the system; (iii) maintenance policy; (iv) vocational training policy; (v) market demand for
higher education; causes of student drop out and repetition in higher education; (vi) conception of
evaluation instruments; (vii) creation of a small/efficient labor market observatory; and (viii) design of the
various grant mechanisms including operational manuals; (c) technical assistance for: (i) Early Childhood
planning, implementation, testing and development; (ii) pre-service and in-service teacher training at the
primary and secondary levels; (iii) curricula development; (iv) textbook manuscript development; (v)
teacher career management; and (vi) information system (MIS-GIS) development; (d) twinning
arrangements with intemational institutions for knowledge transfer and technical assistance in the areas of:
(i) student learning assessment; (ii) primary curriculum and textbook conception; (iii) secondary curriculum
development; (iv) "recherche-action" development; (v) development and implementation of new TVT
modules; and (vi) assessment of the existing higher education 'fili&res" and development of new
professionally oriented ones, and Faculty management under Agreements between Faculties and MEN; (e)
IEC activities related to ECD, primary education, literacy and vocational training; (f) capacity building for
school management; (g) training for managers, teachers and trainers; (h) project management including
procurement and accounting specialists; and (i) technical and financial audits.
25.   Procurement methods. The standard method of selection will be competition among qualified firms
short-listed on the basis of replies to a Request for Expression of Interest, based on the Quality-and
Cost-Based Selection (QCBS). As much as practicable, training institutions will be selected on the
Consultant's Qualification (CQ) method. For the financial audit contract (of a standard nature) the
Least-Cost Selection will be the most appropriate method. Services of trainers, lecturers and researchers,
small studies, as well as professional staff for the implementation units, that can be provided by Individual
Consultants (estimated to cost less than US$ 50,000 equivalent per contract and up to aggregate amount of
US$ 1,87 million equivalent), will be selected through comparison of their qualifications for the assignment,
on the basis of CVs and references, among those expressing interest in the assignment or approached
directly, in accordance with part V of the Guidelines. When the estimated amount is greater than
US$200,000 equivalent, a Request for Expression of Interest will be published in a national newspaper and
in the UN Development Business. Short lists of consultants for contracts estimated under US$ 100,000
equivalent may comprise only national consultant firms in accordance with section 2.7 of the Consultant
Guidelines, provided that a sufficient number of qualified firms (at least three) are available at competitive
costs, and foreign consultants who have expressed interest are not excluded. Contracts with UN agencies
will be in accordance with paragraphs 3.13 and 3.15 of the Guidelines. For training abroad and in-country,
the training program -- containing names of candidates, cost estimates, content of courses, periods of
training, institution selection -- will be reviewed by IDA annually. Single-source selection will be used
exceptionally in the cases mentioned in para. 26 below.
26.    Single-source selection is proposed by the Government for exceptional use in accordance with
paragraphs 3.8-3.11 of the Guidelines for Consultants mainly for reasons of continuity between the
Education V and ESDP projects, for the following contracts: (a) BIEF (Belgium) to provide technical
- 86 -



assistance to the MEN for the experimentation of the new primary and secondary curricula and programs
and support to textbook preparation, because this institution has successfully assisted, under Education V,
the development of these new curricula and textbooks which needs to be immediately followed by the
experimentation; the amount of the contract will be less than the equivalent of US$650,000; (b) NS21
(Canada) to provide technical assistance to the MEN for the support to multigrade teaching because this
assignment is the direct continuation of previous satisfactory support during Education V for a maximumn
amount of US$ 200,000; (c) contract management for civil works will be delegated to AMEXTIPE (for a
contract amount less than US$550,000 equivalent), because if these services performed by an international
firm they would be more expensive, and there is no other local firm with such expertise in contract
management; (d) contracts with the national team of 3 engineers, 3 assistants and 6 drivers (Mauritania)
who successfully assisted communities for the community-based primary classroom construction during the
Education V project will be renewed under ESDP for reason of continuity, with a maximum amount of
US$400,000 equivalent for all team contracts; and (e) contract with the national management team of the
DPEF which has successfully managed previous projects, for reasons of continuity, for a maximum amount
of US$670,000 equivalent.
27.   Grants (total US$24.86 million).
Under the ESDP, the existing grant mechanism for community-based school construction will be continued
with financing from AfDB and IDA. In addition, 6 new grant mechanisms will be created: the School
Performance and Improvement Grants (SPIG); the Private Sector Education Grants (PSEG); the Technical
and Vocational Training Fund (TVTF); the ECD support Grants (ECDG); The Non Formal Education
Grant (NFEG), and the Research Support Grant (RSG).
28.   Grants supported by IDA (total grants US$20.48 million)
(a)    Community-based primary school construction (US$17.74 million equivalent). Under ESDP the
MEN will delegate to communities the primary school construction financed by AfDB and IDA. This
grant-mechanism was successfully set up in 1989 under the Education III project and was continued during
the Education V project. Communities have already built more than 2,500 classrooms. IDA-financed grants
(US$14.42 million equivalent) will support: the construction and furnishing of 1,830 new classrooms and
rehabilitation of 230. Priority will be given to the completion of schools by promoting 3-classroom
multigrade schools, equipping new and retrofitting existing schools with latrines (total 620) and office
storages (about 300). The standard classroom design is simple and the costs are low (about US$5,000 per
classroom). The Government provides grants to communities representing 70% of the estimated cost for
classrooms and 100% for latrines, office-storage bloc, furniture and fencing. Individual grants do not
exceed US$30,000 equivalent. Government's and Communities' responsibilities are embodied in a
contractual agreement signed before works start. Payments from the grants will be made by the DPEF to
the conmnunities in tranches (installments) on the basis of works completed and technically certified by the
DPEF's engineers. Arrangements for the implementation of this grant mechanism are described in the
specific module of the Manual of Procedures called: Manuel de Procedures - Appui aux Collectivites pour
la Construction d'Infrastructures de Base. This Manual is currently operational and is acceptable to IDA.
It was revised during project preparation to incorporate additional detailed community-based procurement
procedures derived from the WB procurement and disbursement manualfor projects with community
participation, issued November 1, 1995. The Government will submit to the Bank the final version of the
revised module of the Manual of Procedures for review.
(b)    School Performance and Improvement Grants - SPIG (US$ 1.1 million equivalent). The ESDP
intends to test decentralized mechanisms for school-based improvement through allocation of two types of
- 87 -



grants depending on the school level (primary or secondary). Grants will be provided by the DPEF to
eligible schools through sub-project Agreements awarded by an Evaluation Committee on a competitive
basis. Individual grants will not exceed US$1,200 and US$2,000 for primary and secondary schools,
respectively. The flow of funds, implementation and accounting arrangements will be governed by a
specific module of the Manual of Procedures which will include detailed description of: (i) procedures for
preparation and submission of sub-project by potential beneficiaries; (ii) eligibility criteria; (iii) appraisal
and approval procedure; (iv) flow of funds chart and disbursement mechanisms; (v) monitoring and
evaluation system including benchmarks and performance indicators based on a planned disbursement
schedule; and (vi) technical and financial audit. Submission by the Borrower of the specific module of the
Manual of Procedures for the management of the SPIG is a condition of disbursement of funds under this
category.
(c)    Private Sector Education Grants - PSEG (US$1.70 million equivalent). The PSEG intends to
promote the private education sector by providing grants to private institutions. Grants will be provided by
the DPEF to eligible private education providers through sub-project Agreements awarded by an
Evaluation Committee on the basis of eligibility criteria defined in the Manual of Procedures. Individual
grants will not exceed US$20,000 equivalent. The flow of funds, implementation and accounting
arrangements will be governed by a specific module of the Manual of Procedures which will include
detailed description of: (i) procedures for preparation and submission of sub-project by potential
beneficiaries; (ii) eligibility criteria; (iii) appraisal and approval procedure; (iv) flow of funds chart and
disbursement mechanisms; (v) monitoring and evaluation system including benchmarks and performance
indicators based on a planned disbursement schedule; (vi) technical and financial audit. Submission by the
Borrower of the specific module of the Manual of Procedures for the management of the PSEG, detailing
procedures for elaboration, submission, appraisal, implementation, financing and evaluation of
sub-projects, acceptable to IDA, is a condition of disbursement of funds under this category.
(d)    The Technical and Vocational Training Fund - (TVTF) (US$1.7 million equivalent) will be created
to provide grants to TVT centers and private enterprises as a mechanism to test a new method to finance
in-service training and apprenticeship mechanisms. Sub-projects proposed by enterprises and training
centers will be of two types: (a) in-Service training in enterprise and (b) apprenticeship dual training.
Individual grants will be provided on a matching basis with the beneficiaries' participation amounting to no
less than 20% of the estimated cost of the sub-project. The grants will be financed by the Government and
IDA on an equal basis (maximum 40% each). Both resources will be managed by DPEF and awarded to
eligible beneficiaries by the Fund's Board whose secretariat will be entrusted to the INP-FTP(MEN). At
start-up, grants will not exceed US$5,000 equivalent for type (a) and US$7,000 equivalent for type (b).
This threshold may be reviewed during annual joint reviews according to experience. Submission by the
Borrower of the specific module of the Manual of Procedures for the management of the TVTF detailing
procedures for elaboration, submission, appraisal, implementation, financing and evaluation of
sub-projects, acceptable to IDA, is a condition of disbursement of funds under this category.
(e)    The ECD Support Grants - (ECDG) (US$0.25 million equivalent) will be created and tested to
provide grant support to communities which have developed an ECD center, with a view to helping them
provide better remuneration for the person in charge of the center and the procurement of small equipment
to facilitate access to such centers. The overall objective is to improve the quality and the stability of the
Centers' personnel hired by the communities. Grants will be channeled by the DPEF and awarded to
eligible communities by an Evaluation Committee on the basis of the criteria defined in a specific module of
the Manual of Procedures. The amount of individual grants will not exceed US$ 1,000 equivalent.
Submission by the Borrower of the specific module of the Manual of Procedures for the management of the
ECDG, acceptable to iDA, is a condition of disbursement of funds under this category.
- 88 -



(f)    The Non Formal Education Grant - (NFEG) (US$0.60 million equivalent). The IDA credit will
finance grants to communities for two different activities: (i) improving Koranic education provided in
mahadras, to include science and language training, through pairing arrangements (one mahadra is paired
with the neighboring formal school) successfully experimented by UNICEF; (ii) testing a new approach for
providing functional literacy programs to demanding communities through grants to private literacy
providers, mainly NGOs, on the basis of sub-projects submitted by literacy providers. Submission by the
Borrower of a specific module in the Manual of Procedures for the management of the NFEG, detailing
procedures for submission, appraisal, implementation, financing and evaluation of sub-projects, acceptable
to IDA, is a condition of disbursement of fuids under this category.
(g)    The Research Support Fund - (RSF) (US$0.80 million equivalent). The IDA credit will finance
university research sub-projects proposed by researchers on a 50/50 matching basis. Research sub-projects
will be prepared and submitted by individual researchers or groups. The Directorate of Higher Education
will be responsible for organizing the grant mechanism. Grants will be awarded by a scientific committee to
researchers from the public and private sector of higher education for eligible research sub-projects on the
basis of criteria spelled out in the Manual of Procedures. The DPEF will be responsible to finance the
research sub-projects to which grants have been awarded. Individual grants will not exceed US$15,000
equivalent. This threshold may be reviewed during the annual review meetings based on actual results.
Submission by the Borrower of the specific module of the Manual of Procedures for the management of the
RSF detailing procedures for elaboration, submission, appraisal, implementation, financing and evaluation
of sub-projects, acceptable to IDA, is a condition of disbursement of funds under this category.
- 89-

Prior review thresholds (Table B)
29.    Prior review thresholds were detenrined on the basis of the procurement capacity assessment.
The review procedures followed will be in accordance with the Appendix I (Review by the Bank) of both
procurement Guidelines. Contracts not subject to prior review will be selectively reviewed during project
implementation. In the event of increases in works contracts of more than 15% of the original price, the
Borrower must specify the reasons and request the Bank's non-objection prior to proceeding with the
additional works.
30. Civil works contracts exceeding the equivalent of US$250,000 and the five first contracts of less than
US$250,000 will be subject to prior review by IDA. For all contracts for works for which there are less
than three bidders, or for any recommendation not to select the lowest evaluated bid, the award proposal
will be submitted to IDA for approval prior to notifying the winning bidder. All other contracts will be
subject to post review by IDA during supervision missions and by auditors.
31.   Goods contracts for an amount exceeding the equivalent of US$100,000 will be subject to prior
review by IDA. All other contracts will be subject to post review during supervision missions and by
auditors.
32.   All contracts with consulting firms exceeding US$100,000 equivalent and with individuals
consultants exceeding US$30,000 equivalent will be subject to prior review. Terms of Reference for all
contracts, single-source hiring, assignments of a critical nature (as determined by IDA, like the financial
audit) will be subject to prior review. For QCBS selection of consultants for contracts above
US$100,000, IDA will review the technical evaluation before opening of the financial proposals.
Procurement supervision and technical audit
33.   Procurement specialists will supervise all executing agencies every six months. During these
missions selective post review (1 out of 5 contracts) will be carried out for contracts awarded below the
ftresholds. AMEXTIPE activities will be subject to the half-year technical audit by qualified consultants,
selected through the competitive process agreed for consultant services.

Frequency of procurement supervision missions proposed: One every six months (includes special

Reinforcement of procurement capacities. Procurement capacity of the Sector will be strengthened by:
(i) reinforcing the procurement capacity of the DPEF by recruitment of two professional staff to be in place
before Credit effectiveness; (ii) reinforcing the procurement capacity of the DAFM; (iii) recruitment of
additional civil servants in the DAFM according to job descriptions included in the PIP; and (iv) organizing
the DAFM's and DPEF's procurement staff to work together so that training of DAFM staff by DPEF will
result in full DAFM procurement capacity built by the end of the first phase. The procurement section of
the procedure manual will include clear job descriptions and performance requirements of the procurement
staff, procurement monitoring and reporting arrangements and other processes related to the procurement
staff. The reinforcement of the procurement capacity of the DAFM is on of the objective of the project, and
is detailed in a specific module of the PIP (module GS2). The procurement team will also benefit from
support provided by the yearly technical and procurement audits. On the basis of the participative
procurement capacity assessment, an action plan for immediate procurement capacity reinforcement was
developed, its schedule was agreed during negotiations.

Disbursement
Allocation of credit proceeds (Table C)
I .    Disbursements of the IDA credit will be made for civil works, goods, consultant services and
training and operating expenses that are eligible for IDA financing. The credit will be disbursed over a
period of 48 months, taking into account that the credit's closing date will be May 31, 2006, corresponding
to six months after the project completion date. While operating under traditional disbursement procedures
all disbursements will be fully documented at the time of submission of withdrawal applications, except for
expenditures made against Statement of Expenditures (SOE). Once the project's financial management is
deemed satisfactory enough to fulfill all the requirements of the Project Management Reports (PMR)-based
disbursements, it is expected that traditional disbursement procedures for this project will be phased out.
The proposal for allocation of IDA Credit funds is given in Table C.

Use of statements of expenditures (SOEs):
3.     All replenishment or reimbursement applications will be submitted monthly or when the SA will be
reduced by one-third, whichever comes first. All replenishment applications will be fully documented
except for: (a) contracts of less than US$100,000 equivalent for goods; (b) contracts of less than
US$250,000 equivalent for works; (c) consulting services provided by individual consultants less than

US$30,000 equivalent; and (d) consulting services provide by consulting firns less than US$100,000
equivalent. SOE documentation will be retained by the DPEF and made available for review as requested
by auditors (including technical audits) and by the World Bank supervision missions.
Special account:
4.    Special Account under Traditional Disbursement Procedures. To facilitate disbursements, the
Government will open a Special Accounts at a commercial bank. The authorized allocation will be:
US$4.0 million equivalent. The authorized allocation will cover four months' eligible expenditures. Upon
effectiveness, an amount representing 50% of the authorized allocations will be deposited in the Special
Account until the aggregate amount of withdrawals from the Credit account plus the total amount of all
outstanding commitments entered into by the Association shall equal or exceed the equivalent of SDR
7,000,000. Replenishment applications will be submitted at least monthly by the DPEF. Each
replenishment request will be accompanied, as necessary, by an up-to-date bank statement and a
reconciliation statement
5.    Special Account for Withdrawal Made on the Basis of PMR. Upon receipt of each application for
withdrawal of an amount of the Credit, the Association shall, on behalf of the Borrower, withdraw from the
Credit Account and deposit into the Special Account an amount equal to the lesser of: (a) the amount so
requested; and (b) the amount which the Association has determined, based on the PMR accompanying said
application, is required to be deposited in order to finance eligible expenditures during the six-month period
following the date of such report; provided, however, that the amount so deposited, when added to the
amount indicated by said PMR to be remaining in the Special Account, shall not exceed the amount of
US$6.0 million.
Counterpart Funds, Project Account
6.    The Government has agreed to deposit in a Project Account opened in a commercial bank an
annual amount equal to the amount of the initial deposit, and to replenish the project account at its initial
level on a quarterly basis to make sure there are sufficient funds to cover counterpart funds. At the time of
negotiations, Government agreed to set up a quarterly replenishable account US$250,000 equivalent, and to
provide a total of US$1 million equivalent per year in the Project account. An initial deposit of
US$250,000 equivalent in the Project Account is a condition of IDA Credit effectiveness. This Project
Account will be managed by the DPEF on terms and conditions agreeable to IDA.
Financial management
7.    Accounting and Financial Reporting. During the first phase of the program, the DPEF will be
responsible for financial management of the ESDP and will maintain the books and accounts. It will also
be responsible for the production of the annual financial statements. The DPEF has a satisfactory financial
and accounting unit. It has gained solid experience in IDA procedures through previous projects (the
General Education Project: Cr. 2706 and the Vocational Training Project: Cr.252 1). However, it will be
strengthened under this project with better performing computer equipment, refresher training and a revised
procedures manual. A local accounting firm with experience in project financial management will be
appointed to review the existing computerized accounting and financial management system, including the
accounting software, based on internationally acceptable accounting principles agreed with the Bank. The
firm will also prepare the accompanying accounting manual, including a proper chart of accounts, the
various transaction cycles, the fornat, content and periodicity of the various financial statements to be
produced, the budgetary procedures and process (preparation, monitoring, variance analysis, etc.), and the
relevant internal controls. The terms of reference have been reviewed and agreed to by IDA. The firn will
- 97 -



be responsible for the initial training of the accounting and financial management staff for the efficient
operation of the new software system. It will also be responsible for the preparation of a training program
in financial management and an implementation timetable for the duration of the project.
8.    Auditing. During negotiations, the Government provided the assurance that: (a) project accounts
will be audited in accordance with international standards by an experienced and internationally recognized
audit firm acceptable to IDA. The audit reports and related project accounts will be submitted to IDA
within six months after the end of Govemment's fiscal year; (b) in addition to their standard short-form
report with opinion, the auditors will be required to: (i) carry out a comprehensive review of all the SOE as
well as the internal control procedures governing their preparation for the relevant period under audit, and
express a separate opinion thereon; and (ii) review the management and utilization of the Special Account
and express a separate opinion thereon as well; (c) the auditor will also finalize the review of the internal
control system of the project with a view to identifying the major weaknesses and shortcomings and
proposing practical recommendations for improvement. The results of this review will be documented in a
Management Letter to be submitted along with the audit report.
9.    The financial auditors will also perform interim audits (in the ninth month of each fiscal year) to
review the internal control system including management performance, and issue reports to that effect
within one month from the end of their work. The findings and recommendations of the interim reports will
be addressed by management without delay before the final audit (within three to four months after closing
of the fiscal year of the project). The contracting of auditors on a multi-year contract, acceptable to IDA,
has already taken place; certification by the financial auditors that the project accounting system is
operational is a condition of credit effectiveness. The IDA credit will only finance audit expenditures under
incremental operating costs.
Monitoring and Reporting
10.   The World Bank is introducing an initiative to change loan administration in the World Bank
Group-financed projects, the Financial Management Initiative (FMI). This initiative assists in putting in
place sound financial management, procurement, and output monitoring systems for projects. Where
appropriate, and when these systems are in place, disbursements may be made on the basis of agreed
quarterly Project Management Reports (PMR) rather than on the basis of individual invoices or SOEs.
11.   During Phase 1, the project will not be considered as being in fill compliance with the FMI for
purposes of disbursements. The following action plan has been established in order to make the project
ready for FMI within 18 months of Credit effectiveness.
